 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:11pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right"><B>Exhibit 99.1 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:18pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>onsemi Reports Record Third Quarter 2022 Results </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>PHOENIX &#150; Oct. 31, 2022 &#150;</B> onsemi (the &#147;Company&#148;) (Nasdaq: ON) today announced results for the third quarter of 2022 with the
following highlights: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="9%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Record revenue of $2,192.6&nbsp;million, an increase of 26&nbsp;percent year-over-year </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="9%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> gross margin of 48.3&nbsp;percent and
49.3&nbsp;percent, respectively </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">GAAP operating margin of 19.4&nbsp;percent </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="9%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Record <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating margin of 35.4&nbsp;percent increased
approximately 1,100 bps year-over-year </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="9%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">GAAP diluted earnings per share of $0.70, flat as compared to the quarter a year ago </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Record <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted earnings per share of $1.45 as compared to $0.87
in the quarter a year ago </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:2pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Free cash flow of $731&nbsp;million and record LTM free cash flow margin of 21.0&nbsp;percent
</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:20pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;onsemi has delivered another quarter of record results stemming from continued growth in our focus markets of automotive and
industrial. We remain confident in our long-term outlook as we continue to win where semiconductor content growth is accelerating for vehicle electrification, energy infrastructure, advanced safety and factory automation. We have taken a proactive
and deliberate approach over the last several quarters to make the structural changes required to strengthen our business and we are in a better position than ever to navigate the current uncertainty in the market.&#148; </P>

vesting of restricted stock units, the incremental dilutive shares from the Company&#146;s convertible senior subordinated notes, and the repurchase or the issuance of stock or convertible notes or the sale of treasury shares. In periods when the
quarterly average stock price per share exceeds $20.72 for the 1.625% Notes and $52.97 for the 0% Notes, the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted share count and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> net income per
share include the anti-dilutive impact of the Company&#146;s hedge transactions issued concurrently with the 1.625% Notes and the 0% Notes, respectively. At an average stock price per share between $20.72 and $30.70 for the 1.625% Notes and $52.97
and $74.34 for the 0% Notes, the hedging activity offsets the potentially dilutive effect of the 1.625% Notes and 0% Notes, respectively. In periods when the quarterly average stock price exceeds $30.70 for the 1.625% Notes, and $74.34 for the 0%
Notes, the dilutive impact of the warrants issued concurrently with such notes are included in the diluted shares outstanding. GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted share counts are based on either the previous
quarter&#146;s average stock price or the stock price as of the last day of the previous quarter, whichever is higher. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:18pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="7%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">**</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="justify">Special items may include: amortization of acquisition-related intangibles; expensing of appraised inventory
fair market value <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">step-up;</FONT> <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> facility costs, purchased <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">in-process</FONT> research and development expenses; restructuring,
asset impairments and other, net; goodwill impairment charges; gains and losses on debt prepayment; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> interest expense; actuarial (gains) losses on pension plans and other pension benefits; and certain
other special items, as necessary. These special items are out of our control and could change significantly from period to period. As a result, we are not able to reasonably estimate and separately present the individual impact or probable
significance of these special items, and we are similarly unable to provide a reconciliation of the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures. The reconciliation that is unavailable would include a forward-looking income statement,
balance sheet and statement of cash flows in accordance with GAAP. For this reason, we use a projected range of the aggregate amount of special items in order to calculate our projected <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating
expense outlook. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">2 </P>

</DIV></Center>

<TD WIDTH="7%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">***</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="justify">We believe these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures provide important supplemental
information to investors. We use these measures, together with GAAP measures, for internal managerial purposes and as a means to evaluate <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">period-to-period</FONT></FONT> comparisons.
However, we do not, and you should not, rely on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures alone as measures of our performance. We believe that <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures reflect an
additional way of viewing aspects of our operations that, when taken together with GAAP results and the reconciliations to corresponding GAAP financial measures that we also provide in our releases, provide a more complete understanding of factors
and trends affecting our business. Because <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures are not standardized, it may not be possible to compare these financial measures with other companies&#146;
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures, even if they have similar names. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>TELECONFERENCE </B></P>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About onsemi </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>onsemi</B> (Nasdaq: <FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" COLOR="#0000ff">ON</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman">) is
driving disruptive innovations to help build a better future. With a focus on automotive and industrial <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">end-markets,</FONT> the company is accelerating change in megatrends such as vehicle electrification and safety,
sustainable energy grids, industrial automation, and 5G and cloud infrastructure. <B>onsemi</B> offers a highly differentiated and innovative product portfolio, delivering intelligent power and sensing technologies that solve the world&#146;s most
complex challenges and leads the way to creating a safer, cleaner, and smarter world. <B>onsemi </B>is recognized as a Fortune 500<SUP STYLE="font-size:75%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP> company and included in the S&amp;P 500<SUP
STYLE="font-size:75%; vertical-align:top">&reg;</SUP> index. Learn more about <B>onsemi</B> at </FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" COLOR="#0000ff">www.onsemi.com</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman">.

<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>RECONCILIATION OF GAAP VERSUS NON-GAAP DISCLOSURES (Continued) </B></P>

</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> MEASURES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">To supplement the consolidated financial results prepared in accordance with GAAP, onsemi uses certain
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures, which are adjusted from the most directly comparable GAAP measures to exclude items related to the amortization of acquisition-related intangibles, expensing of appraised inventory fair
market value <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">step-up,</FONT> inventory valuation adjustments, purchased <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">in-process</FONT> research and development expenses, restructuring, asset impairments and other, net, goodwill
impairment charges, gains and losses on debt prepayment, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> interest expense, actuarial (gains) losses on pension plans and other pension benefits, third party acquisition and divestiture-related costs,
tax impact of these items and certain other <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> items, as necessary. Management does not consider the effects of these items in evaluating the core operational activities of onsemi. Management uses
these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures internally to make strategic decisions, forecast future results and evaluate onsemi&#146;s current performance. In addition, the Company believes that most analysts covering onsemi use
the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures to evaluate onsemi&#146;s performance. Given management&#146;s and other relevant parties&#146; use of these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures, onsemi believes
these measures are important to investors in understanding onsemi&#146;s current and future operating results as seen through the eyes of management. In addition, management believes these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures
are useful to investors in enabling them to better assess changes in onsemi&#146;s core business across different time periods. These <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures are not prepared in accordance with, and should not be
considered alternatives or necessarily superior to, GAAP financial data and may be different from <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures used by other companies. Because <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial
measures are not standardized, it may not be possible to compare these financial measures with other companies&#146; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures, even if they have similar names. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Revenue </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> revenue allows management to evaluate, among other things, the revenue from the
Company&#146;s core businesses and trends across different reporting periods on a consistent basis, independent of special items. In addition, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-</FONT> GAAP revenue is an important component of management&#146;s
internal performance measurement and incentive and reward process as it is used to assess the current and historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, obtaining targets and forecasting future
results. Management presents this <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measure to enable investors and analysts to evaluate the Company&#146;s revenue generation performance relative to the direct costs of operations of
onsemi&#146;s core businesses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Gross Profit and Gross Margin </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> gross profit and gross margin allows management to evaluate, among other things,
the gross margin and gross profit of the Company&#146;s core businesses and trends across different reporting periods on a consistent basis, independent of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> items including, generally speaking,
expensing of appraised inventory fair market value <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">step-up,</FONT> impact of business wind down and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> facility costs. In addition, it is an important component of
management&#146;s internal performance measurement and incentive and reward process as it is used to assess the current and historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, obtaining targets and
forecasting future results. Management presents this <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measure to enable investors and analysts to evaluate our revenue generation performance relative to the direct costs of revenue of
onsemi&#146;s core businesses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Operating Income and Operating Margin </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating income and operating margin allows management to evaluate, among other
things, the operating margin and operating income of the Company&#146;s core businesses and trends across different reporting periods on a consistent basis, independent of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> items including, generally
speaking, expensing of appraised inventory fair market value <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">step-up,</FONT> impact of business wind down, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> facility costs, amortization and impairments of
intangible assets, third party acquisition and divestiture-related costs, restructuring charges and certain other special items as necessary. In addition, it is an important component of management&#146;s internal performance measurement and
incentive and reward process as it is used to assess the current and historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, obtaining targets and forecasting future results. Management presents this <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measure to enable investors and analysts to evaluate the Company&#146;s revenue generation performance relative to the direct costs of operations of onsemi&#146;s core businesses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Net Income Attributable to onsemi and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Diluted Earnings
Per Share </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> net income attributable to onsemi and <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted earnings per share allows management to evaluate the operating results of onsemi&#146;s core businesses and trends across different reporting periods on a consistent basis, independent of <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> items including, generally, the amortization and impairments of intangible assets, expensing of appraised inventory fair market value <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">step-up,</FONT> impact of business wind
down, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-recurring</FONT> facility costs, restructuring, gains and losses on debt prepayment, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> interest expense, actuarial (gains) losses on pension plans and other
pension benefits, </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">11 </P>

</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> MEASURES (Continued) </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">third party acquisition and divestiture-related costs, discrete tax items and other <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> tax
adjustments and certain other special items, as necessary. In addition, these items are important components of management&#146;s internal performance measurement and incentive and reward process, as they are used to assess the current and
historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, setting targets and forecasting future results. Management presents these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures to
enable investors and analysts to understand the results of operations of onsemi&#146;s core businesses and, to the extent comparable, to compare our results of operations on a more consistent basis against those of other companies in our industry.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Free Cash Flow </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use of free
cash flow allows management to evaluate, among other things, the ability of the Company to make interest or principal payments on its debt. Free cash flow is defined as the difference between cash flow from operating activities and capital
expenditures disclosed under investing activities in the consolidated statement of cash flows. Free cash flow is not an alternative to cash flow from operating activities as a measure of liquidity. It is an important component of management&#146;s
internal performance measurement and incentive and reward process as it is used to assess the current and historical financial results of the business and for strategic decision making, preparing budgets, obtaining targets and forecasting future
results. Management presents this <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measure to enable investors and analysts to evaluate our revenue generation performance relative to the direct costs of operations of onsemi&#146;s core
businesses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Diluted Share Count </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="justify">The use of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted share count allows management to evaluate, among other things, the
potential dilution due to the outstanding restricted stock units excluding the dilution from the convertible notes that is covered by hedging activity up to a certain threshold. In periods when the quarterly average stock price per share exceeds
$20.72 for the 1.625% Notes and $52.97 for the 0% Notes, the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> diluted share count includes the anti-dilutive impact of the Company&#146;s hedge transactions issued concurrently with the 1.625% Notes
and the 0% Notes, respectively. At an average stock price per share between $20.72 and $30.70 for the 1.625% Notes and $52.97 and $74.34 for the 0% Notes, the hedging activity offsets the potentially dilutive effect of the 1.625% Notes and 0% Notes,
respectively. In periods when the quarterly average stock price exceeds $30.70 for the 1.625% Notes, and $74.34 for the 0% Notes, the dilutive impact of the warrants issued concurrently with such notes are included in the diluted shares outstanding.
</P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">12 </P>

</DIV></Center>
